TITLE: SAML 2.0 Metadata File Example
DESCRIPTION: An example of a SAML 2.0 metadata file, including entity descriptor, signature, SPSSODescriptor with assertion consumer service details, and organization information. This file is used to configure SAML connections.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: XML
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<md:EntityDescriptor xmlns:md="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:metadata"ID="_9ef5602b6f9ed8b75334f563f91322d2"  
entityID=ENTITY_ID>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
        XML_SIGNATURE  
</ds:Signature>
<md:SPSSODescriptorAuthnRequestsSigned="true"WantAssertionsSigned="true"  
protocolSupportEnumeration="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol">
<md:KeyDescriptoruse="signing">
<ds:KeyInfoxmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
<ds:KeyName>KEY_NAME</ds:KeyName>
<ds:X509Data>
<ds:X509Certificate>
                        X509_ENCODED_CERTIFICATE  
</ds:X509Certificate>
</ds:X509Data>
</ds:KeyInfo>
</md:KeyDescriptor>
<md:AssertionConsumerServiceBinding="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:bindings:HTTP-POST"  
Location="https://*SP_APP_DOMAIN*/saml/acs"index="0"  
isDefault="true"/>  
</md:SPSSODescriptor>
<md:Organization>
<md:OrganizationNamexml:lang="en">ORG_NAME</md:OrganizationName>
<md:OrganizationDisplayNamexml:lang="en">ORG_DISPLAY_NAME</md:OrganizationDisplayName>
<md:OrganizationURLxml:lang="en">ORG_URL</md:OrganizationURL>
</md:Organization>
</md:EntityDescriptor>
```

TITLE: SAML AuthnResponse Example
DESCRIPTION: An example of a SAML AuthnResponse XML structure received after a user successfully logs in using eHerkenning. This response contains assertion details, user attributes, and authentication context.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<saml2p:Response xmlns:saml2p="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol"Destination="https://*SP_APP_DOMAIN*/saml/acs"ID="_8ecbe9dcd8c6e4765d5b6bd9cf5f2010"InResponseTo="_6dee7048f7b558987b5d9900e1b20832"IssueInstant="2023-12-11T12:35:48.235Z"Version="2.0"xmlns:xsd="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema">
<saml2:Issuer xmlns:saml2="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:assertion">https://*YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN*/auth/saml</saml2:Issuer>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
        XML_SIGNATURE
</ds:Signature>
<saml2p:Status>
<saml2p:StatusCodeValue="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:status:Success"/>
</saml2p:Status>
<saml2:Assertion xmlns:saml2="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:assertion"ID="_03c096c04b157811ec2af48c91e4d618"IssueInstant="2023-12-11T12:35:48.263Z"Version="2.0"xmlns:xsd="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema">
<saml2:Issuer>https:/*YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN*/auth/saml</saml2:Issuer>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
            XML_SIGNATURE
</ds:Signature>
<saml2:Subject>
<saml2:NameIDFormat="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:1.1:nameid-format:unspecified"NameQualifier="urn:etoegang:HM:00000003244440010000:entities:9713">k5QDBPNavooSgsxQNCITxSnQc5oo37cqev726-Iz1-Y=</saml2:NameID>
<saml2:SubjectConfirmationMethod="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:cm:bearer">
<saml2:SubjectConfirmationDataInResponseTo="_6dee7048f7b558987b5d9900e1b20832"NotOnOrAfter="2023-12-11T12:37:48.263Z"Recipient="https://*SP_APP_DOMAIN*/saml/acs"/>
</saml2:SubjectConfirmation>
</saml2:Subject>
<saml2:ConditionsNotBefore="2023-12-11T12:35:43.263Z"NotOnOrAfter="2023-12-11T12:37:48.263Z">
<saml2:AudienceRestriction>
<saml2:Audience>ENTITY_ID</saml2:Audience>
</saml2:AudienceRestriction>

<saml2:AttributeStatement>
<saml2:AttributeName="name">
<saml2:AttributeValuexmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"xsi:type="xsd:string">Gerarda Josephina Kierkegaard</saml2:AttributeValue>

<saml2:AttributeName="firstName">
<saml2:AttributeValuexmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"xsi:type="xsd:string">Gerarda Josephina</saml2:AttributeValue>

<saml2:AttributeName="lastName">
<saml2:AttributeValuexmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"xsi:type="xsd:string">Kierkegaard</saml2:AttributeValue>
</saml2:Attribute>
<saml2:AttributeName="email">
<saml2:AttributeValuexmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"xsi:type="xsd:string">email@example.com</saml2:AttributeValue>
</saml2:Attribute>
<saml2:AttributeName="pseudo">
<saml2:AttributeValuexmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"xsi:type="xsd:string">03659FB1FAE5D26DB2D28866C1A4FE7F4E1CD5E62DD2552EE3D3B11D4C27163D@9162F54B3B07284AC4E147A849DEAEE4</saml2:AttributeValue>

<saml2:AttributeName="kvkNr">
<saml2:AttributeValuexmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"xsi:type="xsd:string">24444001</saml2:AttributeValue>

TITLE: SAML AuthnRequest Example (POST Binding)
DESCRIPTION: An example of a minimal SAML AuthnRequest XML structure used for authentication requests, typically transmitted via POST binding. This request includes essential elements like Issuer and Signature.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<saml2p:AuthnRequest xmlns:saml2p="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol"AttributeConsumingServiceIndex="1"
Destination="https://*YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN*/auth/saml/login"ForceAuthn="true"
ID="_b6a016332e19a825bb42917c9870c93a"IssueInstant="2021-03-09T10:26:17.210Z"
Version="2.0">
<saml2:Issuer xmlns:saml2="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:assertion">
        ENTITY_ID
</saml2:Issuer>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="https://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
        XML_SIGNATURE
</ds:Signature>
</saml2p:AuthnRequest>
```

TITLE: MitID Overview and Integration
DESCRIPTION: Provides an overview of MitID, its use cases, supported protocols, and key attributes. It also links to detailed integration guides and setup procedures.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
MitID:
  Description: A Danish electronic ID replacing NemID, used for identity proofing, authentication, and electronic signing.
  Region: Denmark, Greenland
  Use Cases:
    - Identity Proofing
    - Authentication
    - Electronic Signing
  Supported Protocols:
    - OIDC
    - Authentication REST API
  Devices:
    - Mobile
    - Desktop
  Key Attributes:
    - Name
    - Birthdate
    - National Identity Number
  Levels of Assurance (LoA):
    - High
    - Substantial
    - Low

Integration Steps:
  1. Initial Preparations:
     - Sign agreements.
     - Setup in Dashboard.
     - Select protocol.
     - Link: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/integration-guide/prerequisites/
  2. Integration Guide:
     - Step-by-step guides for connecting via chosen authentication protocol.
     - Link: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/integration-guide/
  3. App Switching on Mobiles:
     - Instructions on how to switch from a native mobile app to the MitID app.
     - Link: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/integration-guide/app-switching/
  4. Attributes Reference:
     - Overview of attributes and claims per protocol.
     - Link: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/attributes-reference/

Testing:
  - Test in Dashboard: Use your sandbox account before integrating.
  - Link: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/test/
```

TITLE: DigiD Production Setup Guide
DESCRIPTION: This documentation outlines the steps required to integrate DigiD for production use. It includes creating a production account, uploading PKI certificates, configuring DigiD in the Signicat Dashboard, obtaining Signicat metadata, requesting DigiD in production, setting up connections with protocols, activating the connection, seeking Logius approval, and conducting audits.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/digid/integration/production

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
DigiD Production Setup:

1. Prerequisites:
   - Ensure all necessary prerequisites are met before starting the production setup.

2. Create a Production Account:
   - Obtain or create a production account for DigiD integration.
   - Add a custom domain if required for your setup.

3. Upload PKI Certificates:
   - Upload the necessary PKI certificates for your DigiD integration.

4. Add DigiD in the Dashboard:
   - Configure DigiD within the Signicat Dashboard.
   - Set up eID configuration details.

5. Get Signicat Metadata:
   - Retrieve the Signicat metadata required for the integration.

6. Request DigiD in Production:
   - Submit a request for DigiD in the production environment.

7. Set up a Connection with a Protocol:
   - Choose a suitable protocol for the connection (e.g., OpenID Connect, SAML).
   - Configure the chosen protocol with the necessary parameters.
   - Define data and attributes to be exchanged.

8. Activate Your Connection:
   - Activate the configured connection to enable DigiD services.

9. Ask Logius to Approve Your Connection:
   - Request approval from Logius for your DigiD connection.

10. Audit and Assessment:
    - Conduct necessary audits and assessments to ensure compliance and functionality.
```

TITLE: Signicat API: Start Verification Process
DESCRIPTION: Initiates an identity verification process using the Signicat API. This endpoint is crucial for starting the verification flow after initial setup and consent.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/id-document-and-biometric-verification/provider-specific-integrations/onfido

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  /processes/startVerification:
    post:
      summary: Start verification
      description: Starts a verification of the identity document that was uploaded.
      parameters:
        - name: dossierId
          in: query
          required: true
          schema:
            type: string
          description: The ID of the dossier.
        - name: processId
          in: query
          required: true
          schema:
            type: string
          description: The ID of the process.
      responses:
        '200':
          description: Verification started successfully.
        '400':
          description: Bad request, e.g., missing parameters or invalid consent.
        '500':
          description: Internal server error.
```

TITLE: Fetch User Profile Script Example
DESCRIPTION: An example Node.js script for fetching user profile information from a UserInfo URL using an access token.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/connectors/auth0-integration

LANGUAGE: Node.js
CODE:
```
// Example Node.js script for Fetch User Profile
// This script would typically be part of the Auth0 custom social connection configuration.

// Assume 'accessToken' is provided by Auth0 and 'userInfoUrl' is configured.

// Example using fetch (requires Node.js 18+ or a polyfill)
async function fetchUserProfile(accessToken, userInfoUrl) {
  try {
    const response = await fetch(userInfoUrl, {
      headers: {
        'Authorization': `Bearer ${accessToken}`
      }
    });

    if (!response.ok) {
      throw new Error(`HTTP error! status: ${response.status}`);
    }

    const profileData = await response.json();
    // Process profileData to extract desired claims
    // For example, mapping Signicat claims to Auth0 user profile attributes
    return {
      name: profileData.name,
      email: profileData.email,
      // ... other claims
    };
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error fetching user profile:', error);
    throw error; // Re-throw to indicate failure to Auth0
  }
}

// In Auth0's context, this function might be called like:
// fetchUserProfile(userinfo.access_token, configuration.USERINFO_URL)
// The return value should be an object mapping to Auth0 user profile properties.
```

TITLE: OIDC Client Setup Guide
DESCRIPTION: This documentation outlines the process of setting up an OpenID Connect (OIDC) client in the Signicat Dashboard. It details the creation and configuration of a client, including obtaining a Client ID and managing associated secrets for different authentication flows. This is a prerequisite for integrating with the Signicat eID Hub for user authentication.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/oidc/oidc-client

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Set up an OIDC client:

Before you can start authenticating users, you must register an OIDC client in the Signicat Dashboard. An OIDC client comes with a Client ID. Depending on the authentication grant type (flow) you want to implement, you can associate a secret to the client.

On this page, you'll find instructions to set up an OIDC client in the Dashboard. You'll learn how to create and configure a client and prepare yourself to connect to eIDs through the Signicat eID Hub. You can also watch a video that shows how to set up an OIDC client in the [Tutorial videos](https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/oidc/oidc-client/#tutorial-videos) section.
```

TITLE: Signicat Authentication REST API Documentation
DESCRIPTION: Documentation for Signicat's Authentication REST API, used for integrating with eID Hub. Supports redirect and headless integration flows.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Signicat Authentication REST API:
  Overview:
    - Provides a flexible way to integrate with eID Hub.
    - Supports both headless and redirect integration flows.
    - Acts as a message broker between your application and eIDs.
  Protocols Supported:
    - OpenID Connect (OIDC)
    - SAML 2.0
    - Signicat's Authentication REST API
  Integration Choice:
    - OIDC: Recommended industry standard, focuses on authentication, uses REST and JSON, manages user sessions.
    - SAML 2.0: More complex, relies on XML, may require a federation agent.
    - Authentication REST API: Developed by Signicat, offers flexibility, supports headless and redirect flows.
  Resources:
    - Detailed guide: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/eid-hub/
```

TITLE: Authorization Code Flow (Basic) - OIDC
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates the basic Authorization Code Flow for setting up authentication with Signicat's OIDC services. It guides users through the initial steps of the authentication process.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/oidc/code-examples

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Endpoint: /oidc/authorize
Method: GET
Description: Initiates the authorization code flow.
Parameters:
  - client_id (string, required): Your application's client ID.
  - redirect_uri (string, required): The URI to redirect to after authorization.
  - response_type (string, required): Must be 'code'.
  - scope (string, required): The requested scopes (e.g., 'openid email profile').
  - state (string, optional): An opaque value used to maintain state between the request and callback.
  - nonce (string, optional): A string value used to associate a client session with an ID Token, and to mitigate replay attacks.

Example:
GET /oidc/authorize?client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&redirect_uri=YOUR_REDIRECT_URI&response_type=code&scope=openid%20email%20profile&state=OPTIONAL_STATE&nonce=OPTIONAL_NONCE
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Endpoint: /oidc/token
Method: POST
Description: Exchanges an authorization code for an access token.
Parameters:
  - grant_type (string, required): Must be 'authorization_code'.
  - code (string, required): The authorization code received from the /authorize endpoint.
  - redirect_uri (string, required): The same redirect URI used in the authorization request.
  - client_id (string, required): Your application's client ID.
  - client_secret (string, required): Your application's client secret.

Example:
POST /oidc/token
Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded

client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&client_secret=YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET&grant_type=authorization_code&code=AUTHORIZATION_CODE&redirect_uri=YOUR_REDIRECT_URI
```

TITLE: Get Session Status
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves the current status of an authentication session using the session ID obtained from creating a new session. Returns user data upon successful authentication.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
GET /sessions/{sessionId}

Response Body (on success):
{
  "status": "SUCCESS",
  "subject": {
    "name": "<user_name>",
    "dateOfBirth": "<user_dob>",
    "nin": "<user_nin>"
  }
}
```

TITLE: Authentication Vault Setup Steps
DESCRIPTION: Provides a step-by-step guide to enable and configure the Authentication Vault within the Signicat Dashboard. This includes navigating to the eID Hub products and setting specific attributes for the vault.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/authentication-vault

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Authentication Vault Setup:

1. Navigate to Dashboard > Products > eID Hub.
2. Select 'Authentication Vault' from the left sidebar.
3. Configure the following attributes on the Authentication Vault page:
   - Obfuscate national identity number
   - Limit storage to specific eIDs
   - Decide record storage duration
4. Select 'Save' to activate the Authentication Vault.
```

TITLE: Create Authentication Session
DESCRIPTION: Initiates an authentication flow by creating a new session. Requires specifying the flow type, requested user attributes, callback URLs for different outcomes, and allowed identity providers.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
POST /sessions

Request Body:
{
  "flow": "redirect",
  "requestedAttributes": [
    "name",
    "dateOfBirth",
    "nin"
  ],
  "callbackUrls": {
    "success": "https://example.com/success",
    "abort": "https://example.com/abort",
    "error": "https://example.com/error"
  },
  "allowedProviders": [
    "nbid"
  ]
}

Response Body (on success):
{
  "sessionId": "<session_id>",
  "authenticationUrl": "<authentication_url>"
}
```

TITLE: Signicat SAML 2.0 URL Metadata Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Configures SAML 2.0 metadata using a dynamic URL hosted on your server. This method requires providing a URL where Signicat can fetch the metadata. It involves specifying connection details, the metadata URL, and optionally mapping assurance levels and attributes.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  Method: POST
  Endpoint: /products/eID Hub/SAML 2.0
  Description: Add new SAML 2.0 configuration using URL method.
  Parameters:
    Name (string, required): Name of the connection.
    Application URL (string, optional): URL of your application.
    Metadata URL (string, required): The web address where you host the metadata.
    Select a LoA contract (string, required): Mapping between levels of assurance.
    Select attribute filter (string, optional): Controls attributes included/excluded in the response.
    Response attribute mapping (object, optional): Customizes attribute names in the response body.
  Example:
    POST /products/eID Hub/SAML 2.0
    {
      "configurationMethod": "URL",
      "name": "MyApplicationConnection",
      "applicationUrl": "https://myapp.com/callback",
      "metadataUrl": "https://myserver.com/metadata.xml",
      "loaContract": "DefaultLoAContract",
      "attributeFilter": "BasicAttributes"
    }
  Notes:
    - Contact support to validate the Metadata URL before adding.
    - Download Signicat's metadata XML after successful configuration.
```

TITLE: Signicat SAML 2.0 Static Form Metadata Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Configures SAML 2.0 metadata by uploading a metadata file or using a form to generate it directly in the Signicat Dashboard. This method is suitable when you don't have a pre-hosted metadata file.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  Method: POST
  Endpoint: /products/eID Hub/SAML 2.0
  Description: Add new SAML 2.0 configuration using Form method.
  Parameters:
    Name (string, required): Name of the connection.
    Metadata File (file, optional): Upload your metadata file here.
    If no file is provided, use the form fields to generate metadata:
      - Entity ID (string, required)
      - Single Sign-On Service URL (string, required)
      - Single Logout Service URL (string, optional)
      - Signing Certificate (string, required, PEM format)
    Select a LoA contract (string, required): Mapping between levels of assurance.
    Select attribute filter (string, optional): Controls attributes included/excluded in the response.
    Response attribute mapping (object, optional): Customizes attribute names in the response body.
  Example:
    POST /products/eID Hub/SAML 2.0
    Content-Type: multipart/form-data
    {
      "configurationMethod": "Form",
      "name": "MyApplicationConnectionStatic",
      "metadataFile": "<metadata_xml_content>",
      "loaContract": "DefaultLoAContract"
    }
  Notes:
    - If not uploading a file, ensure all required form fields are correctly filled.
    - Download Signicat's metadata XML after successful configuration.
```

TITLE: Start Onboarding
DESCRIPTION: The Start onboarding endpoint initiates an onboarding session. This process includes creating a MobileID user, activating a MobileID device, performing a VideoID proofing, and adding identity attributes to the MobileID user.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/reuseid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Start onboarding 
The **Start onboarding** endpoint initiates an onboarding session.
In this flow, you will:
  1. Create a MobileID user.
  2. Activate a MobileID device.
  3. Perform a VideoID proofing.
  4. Add identity attributes to the MobileID user.
```

TITLE: OIDC Authentication URI Example
DESCRIPTION: An example of an OpenID Connect (OIDC) authentication URI used to initiate an FTN authentication flow with Signicat. This URI includes parameters like client ID, response type, scopes, prompt, ACR values, and redirect URI.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/ftn/integration-guide/oidc-ftn

LANGUAGE: HTTP
CODE:
```
https://<YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN>/auth/open/connect/authorize?  
client_id=sandbox-example-client-123  
&response_type=code  
&scope=openid profile idp-id nin ftn-extra  
&prompt=login  
&acr_values=idp:ftn  
&redirect_uri=https://myservice.example/redirect  

```

TITLE: SAML Authentication Flow
DESCRIPTION: Describes the SAML authentication process between a service provider (your app) and an identity provider. It involves the exchange of an AuthnRequest and an AuthnResponse for end-user authentication.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
SAML Authentication Flow:
1. Request: AuthnRequest (sent from Service Provider to Identity Provider)
2. Response: AuthnResponse (sent from Identity Provider to Service Provider)

This process is initiated when an end-user wants to authenticate to your services over a SAML connection.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Signicat Form Configuration Fields
DESCRIPTION: Defines the required and optional fields for configuring SAML connections in the Signicat Dashboard. Includes details on Name, Application URL, Entity ID, Level of Assurance contracts, assertion signing, NameID format, SAML assertion inclusion, assertion encryption, assertion consuming services, single logout services, artifact resolution services, attribute consuming services, certificates, client organization, hosting party organization, contact people, response attribute mappings, attribute filters, and default eID rules.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/quick-start

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Name*: Name of the connection.
Application URL: URL of your application.
Entity ID*: Unique identifier for the connection.
Select a LoA contract*: Select the mapping between levels of assurance that must apply to this configuration. See [Level of Assurance contracts](https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/saml-2-0/saml-loa-contracts/) for more information.
Want assertions signed: If ticked, assertions will be signed.
Use a transient format for the NameID: Tick this box if you only want a transient NameID.
Include the SAML Assertion of the IdentityProvider if available: If the eIDs that you use are SAML-based, you may opt to receive the original SAML assertion of the eID.
Encrypt assertion: If you want to receive an `EncryptedAssertion` instead of an `Assertion` for added security, select this option. Note that some eIDs require you to receive an `EncryptedAssertion`.
Assertion consuming services*: At least one assertion consuming service must be configured. Provide a location URL and a binding type (`REDIRECT`, `POST` or `ARTIFACT`).
Single logout services: Enter the location URL and binding type (`REDIRECT`, `POST` or `ARTIFACT`) of any applicable single logout services.
Artifact resolution services: Enter the location URL, binding type and index of any applicable artifact resolution services.
Attribute consuming services: Enter name, index, description (optional) and at least one attribute
Certificate*: Upload all relevant certificates for the connection (at least one). Information about the certificates, such as issuer and expiration date, is displayed when they are uploaded.
Client organisation: Enter organisation name, display name, and URL.
Hosting party organisation: Provide organisation name, display name, and URL.
Contact people: Provide details about the contact people in your organisation. In **Type of contact person** , specify whether they are part of support, a technical department, name, phone number, and more.
Response attribute mappings: You can customise the name of the attributes received in the response body. You can provide none or many name-to-name mappings.
Select attribute filter: Select an attribute filter to control which attributes you want to include, or exclude, from the response. To create attribute filters in the Dashboard, navigate to **Products** > **eID Hub** > **Advanced** > [**Attribute filters**](https://dashboard.signicat.com/bca/attribute-filters).
Select default eID rule: Select which eID rule to use by default. To add eID rules in the Dashboard, navigate to **Products** > **eID Hub** > **Advanced** > [**eID Rules**](https://dashboard.signicat.com/bca/eid-rules/).
```

TITLE: Dossier Download API Endpoints
DESCRIPTION: Details the GET endpoint for downloading dossier processes, including response codes and example request/response structures.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/id-document-and-biometric-verification

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
GET /dossiers/{dossierId}/processes/{processId}/download
Server URL: https://api.signicat.com/assure/dossiers/{dossierId}/processes/{processId}/download

Responses:
  200 OK: The zip file was successfully created and retrieved.
  204 No Content: The process is not completed or the contents are not yet available for download.
  401 Unauthorized: The Bearer token provided in the Authorization header was not valid.
  404 Not Found: The resource requested cannot be found.

Example Response (401):
{
  "instance": "/assure/dossiers/",
  "method": "POST",
  "status": 401,
  "type": "base:client-problem",
  "title": "The signature of the JWT could not be validated because the key was not found.",
  "detail": "The given JWT is signed by a key with key ID 'signing-key-aaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaa', but no such key was found.",
  "traceId": "034fb8bbc5da31f4dd2cf66e70ef313c"
}
```

TITLE: Signicat API Reference Guide
DESCRIPTION: Provides a comprehensive reference for Signicat's APIs, covering various identity and signing functionalities. This guide is essential for integrating Signicat services into your applications.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/sbid/demo-sbid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  eID Hub API Reference:
    Description: Provides access to various electronic identification (eID) methods.
    Endpoints:
      - /eids: Retrieve a list of available eIDs.
      - /eids/{eidId}: Get details for a specific eID.
      - /authenticate: Initiate an authentication flow.
      - /sign: Initiate a signing process.
    Methods:
      GET /eids
        Description: Retrieves a list of all supported eIDs.
        Parameters:
          - None
        Returns:
          - Array of eID objects, each containing id, name, and description.
      GET /eids/{eidId}
        Description: Retrieves detailed information about a specific eID.
        Parameters:
          - eidId (string, required): The unique identifier of the eID.
        Returns:
          - eID object with detailed properties.
      POST /authenticate
        Description: Initiates an authentication process with a selected eID.
        Parameters:
          - eidId (string, required): The ID of the eID to use for authentication.
          - callbackUrl (string, required): The URL to redirect to after authentication.
          - attributes (array of strings, optional): List of attributes to request from the user.
        Returns:
          - Authentication object with a unique transactionId and a redirect URL.
      POST /sign
        Description: Initiates a signing process for a document.
        Parameters:
          - documentId (string, required): The ID of the document to be signed.
          - eidId (string, required): The ID of the eID to use for signing.
          - callbackUrl (string, required): The URL to redirect to after signing.
        Returns:
          - Signing object with a unique transactionId and a redirect URL.
    Error Conditions:
      - Invalid eidId: Returns 404 Not Found.
      - Missing required parameters: Returns 400 Bad Request.
      - Authentication/Signing failure: Returns 400 Bad Request with an error message.
```

  Service Details:
    Get Process: Retrieves information about a specific process.
    Files in Dossier: Accesses files associated with a dossier.
    Start Capture Flow: Initiates a capture flow for identity verification.
    Images: Manages and retrieves images related to verification.
    Download Full Result: Downloads the complete verification result.
    Matching: Performs matching operations on verification data.
    Redact Images: Enables redaction of sensitive information from images.

    Events (Callbacks): Manages callback events for asynchronous updates.

Destination="https://*YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN*/auth/saml/login"ForceAuthn="true"  
ID="_b6a016332e19a825bb42917c9870c93a"IssueInstant="2021-03-09T10:26:17.210Z"  
Version="2.0">

        ENTITY_ID  
</saml2:Issuer>

</ds:Signature>  
</saml2p:AuthnRequest>

TITLE: Initialize and Run Onfido SDK (Swift)
DESCRIPTION: This code snippet shows how to initialize and run the Onfido SDK in a Swift iOS application. It includes setting the SDK token, configuring steps like welcome, document, and face verification, and handling the SDK response.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/id-document-and-biometric-verification/provider-specific-integrations/onfido

LANGUAGE: Swift
CODE:
```
import UIKit
import Onfido

final class ViewController: UIViewController {

    let authorization: String

    init(authorization: String) {
        self.authorization = authorization
        super.init()
    }

    override func viewDidLoad() {
        super.viewDidLoad()
        self.runFlow(authorization: self.authorization)
    }

    private func runFlow(authorization: String) {
        let responseHandler: (OnfidoResponse) -> Void = {
            response in
            if case let OnfidoResponse.error(innerError) = response {
                print(innerError)
            } else if case OnfidoResponse.success = response {
                print("Success")
            } else if case OnfidoResponse.cancel = response {
                print("Canceled by user")
            }
        }

        let faceStep = FaceStepVariant.photo(withConfiguration: PhotoStepConfiguration())

        let config = try! OnfidoConfig.builder()
            .withSDKToken(authorization)
            .withWelcomeStep()
            .withDocumentStep()
            .withFaceStep(ofVariant: faceStep)
            .build()

        let onfidoFlow = OnfidoFlow(withConfiguration: config)
            .with(responseHandler: responseHandler)

        do {
            let onfidoRun = try onfidoFlow.run()
            onfidoRun.modalPresentationStyle = .formSheet // to present modally
            self.present(onfidoRun, animated: true, completion: nil)
        } catch let error {
            // cannot execute the flow
            // check CameraPermissions
            print(error)
        }
    }
}
```

TITLE: Signicat Authentication API - CreateSession Endpoint
DESCRIPTION: Documentation for the CreateSession endpoint used to start an authentication flow. It details the request method, URL, and the purpose of the endpoint in generating an authentication URL.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/ftn/integration-guide/rest-api-ftn

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
POST https://api.signicat.com/auth/rest/sessions?signicat-accountId={accountId}

Description:
  Initiates an authentication session. The response contains an authentication URL to redirect the end-user.

Parameters:
  accountId (path parameter): Your Signicat account ID.

Request Body:
  (See example JSON for FTN Authentication Request)
  - allowedProviders: List of allowed identity providers (e.g., ["ftn"]).
  - flow: The authentication flow type (e.g., "redirect").
  - requestedAttributes: List of attributes to request from the user.
  - additionalParameters: Provider-specific additional parameters.
  - callbackUrls: URLs for success, abort, and error.
  - encryptionPublicKey: Public key details for encrypting responses (required for FTN).
    - alg: Encryption algorithm (e.g., "RSA-OAEP").
    - e: RSA public exponent.
    - kid: Key ID.
    - kty: Key type (e.g., "RSA").
    - n: RSA modulus.
    - use: Key usage (e.g., "enc").

Response:
  Upon successful request, a session is created, and the response will contain an authentication URL.

Related Endpoints:
  - GetSession: To retrieve the status and results of an ongoing or completed session.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Signicat Authentication REST API
DESCRIPTION: The Signicat Authentication REST API offers flexibility and ease of setup for authentication protocols. It is recommended over SAML 2.0 due to its complexity.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/digid/integration/setup

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Signicat Authentication REST API:
  - Protocol: REST API
  - Description: Provides high flexibility and is easy to set up.
  - Use Case: Recommended for authentication flows where user session management is handled by the developer.
```

TITLE: SAML 2.0 Authentication Request
DESCRIPTION: API documentation for the SAML 2.0 AuthnRequest used to initiate authentication. It details the necessary parameters and structure for a successful request.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/saml-2-0/saml-examples

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
AuthnRequest:
  Purpose: Initiates an authentication process with Signicat.
  Protocol: SAML 2.0
  Method: POST (typically)
  Parameters:
    - AttributeConsumingServiceIndex: (Optional) Specifies the index of the attribute consuming service.
    - Destination: The URL where the request should be sent (Signicat's login endpoint).
    - ForceAuthn: (Optional) If true, forces the Identity Provider to re-authenticate the user.
    - ID: A unique identifier for the request.
    - IssueInstant: The timestamp when the request was issued.
    - Version: The SAML version (e.g., "2.0").
  Elements:
    - saml2:Issuer: Contains the Entity ID of the service provider.
    - ds:Signature: Contains the XML signature for the request.
  Example:
    See the 'AuthnRequest basic example' for a code snippet.
```

TITLE: Signicat Email OTP Configuration Prerequisites
DESCRIPTION: Details the necessary steps and prerequisites for configuring the Signicat Email OTP service. This includes account creation, organization setup, and domain configuration within the Signicat Dashboard.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/email-otp/setup/configuration

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Signicat Dashboard Setup:
  1. Sign up for a Signicat account and register your profile.
     - Refer to: Get started with Signicat guide.
  2. Set up an organisation within the Dashboard.
     - Refer to: Organisation Management - Organisations.
  3. Set up an account within the Dashboard.
     - Refer to: Organisation Management - Accounts.
  4. Configure a domain for Email OTP usage.
     - Refer to: Organisation Management - Domains.

Testing Recommendation:
  - Create a sandbox account for testing services before going live.
  - Sandbox and production accounts require separate setup.
```

TITLE: AuthnRequest with Redirect Binding and Prefilled Attributes
DESCRIPTION: This example shows an AuthnRequest using the REDIRECT binding, including prefilled attributes like first name and email for a streamlined authentication process.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/saml-2-0/saml-examples

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<saml2p:AuthnRequest xmlns:saml2p="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol"AttributeConsumingServiceIndex="1"
Destination="https://*YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN*/auth/saml/login"ForceAuthn="true"
ID="_b6a016332e19a825bb42917c9870c93a"IssueInstant="2021-03-09T10:26:17.210Z"
Version="2.0">
<saml2:Issuer xmlns:saml2="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:assertion">
        ENTITY_ID
</saml2:Issuer>
<samlp:Extensions>
<req-attr:RequestedAttributes>
<md:RequestedAttributeisRequired="true"
Name="firstName"/>
            ...
<md:RequestedAttributeName="signicat:prefilled:email">
<saml:AttributeValue xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"xsi:type="xs:string">subject@example.com</saml:AttributeValue>
</md:RequestedAttribute>
<md:RequestedAttributeisRequired="false"
Name="signicat:prefilled:mobile">
<saml:AttributeValue xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"xsi:type="xs:string">1234567890</saml:AttributeValue>
</md:RequestedAttribute>
</req-attr:RequestedAttributes>
</samlp:Extensions>
</saml2p:AuthnRequest>
```

TITLE: AuthnRequest with IdP Scoping
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to use IdP scoping in a SAML 2.0 AuthnRequest to specify which Identity Providers (eIDs) are available for user authentication.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/saml-2-0/saml-examples

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<saml2p:AuthnRequest xmlns:saml2p="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol"AttributeConsumingServiceIndex="1"
Destination="https://*YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN*/auth/saml/login"ForceAuthn="false"
ID="_aeaf5a7ddbc280bde07a1024f0574b70"IssueInstant="2021-03-09T10:47:58.502Z"Version="2.0">
<saml2:Issuer xmlns:saml2="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:assertion">
        ENTITY_ID
</saml2:Issuer>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
        XML_SIGNATURE
</ds:Signature>
<saml2p:Scoping>
<saml2p:IDPList>
<saml2p:IDPEntryProviderID="ftn"/>
</saml2p:IDPList>
</saml2p:Scoping>
</saml2p:AuthnRequest>
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Transaction Data Fields
DESCRIPTION: Details the data fields available for each transaction, including their descriptions and examples. Covers fields like Date, Usage type, Method name, Product, Invoiced, Completed, Started, Loaded, and Failed.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/billing-and-analytics/transactions

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Transaction Data Fields:

- Date: The date of the transaction.
- Usage type: Information about what product is being used for the transaction.
  - Example (migrated): `srn:sue:1:authbroker:nbid:auth`
  - Example (not-migrated): `com.signicat.services.nbidjs.authentication.method`
- Method name: The name of the method used. This field is only shown if not included in the _Usage type_.
  - Example: nbid
- Product: The name of the product being used from Signicat.
  - Example: Norwegian BankID High - Authentications
- Invoiced: 
  - CPQ: The total number of transactions with status _Invoiced_.
  - Legacy: This is always `0`. You need to check the invoice for information.
- Completed: The total number of transactions with status _Completed_.
- Started: The total number of transactions with status _Started_.
- Loaded: The total number transactions with status _Loaded_.
- Failed: The total number of transactions with status _Failed_.
```

TITLE: Start Verification Process
DESCRIPTION: Initiates a verification process for a given dossier and process ID. Supports FaceTec enrollment and specifies image depiction. Requires dossierId and processId in the path.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/id-document-and-biometric-verification

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
POST /dossiers/{dossierId}/processes/{processId}

Server URL: https://api.signicat.com/assure/dossiers/{dossierId}/processes/{processId}

Path Parameters:
- dossierId (string, required): This ID is obtained from the "Create dossier" response body. Example: 37191afe-25b3-4c30-b42a-b0ab64aa1d64
- processId (string, required): `processId` is obtained from the "Create process" response body. Example: 8afb3ac6-6780-42e4-bbc2-3713e2f6d97c

Request Body Schema (application/json):
Start verification payload
- facetecEnrollment (object, optional): This field only applies to the 'facetec' provider and is required. This object contains necessary information to validate the liveness of a person. The FaceTec SDK provides the returned values of these liveness checks. The values are matched against `imageDepiction`.
  - faceScan (string, required): Face scan data.
  - auditTrailImage (string, required): Audit trail image data.
  - lowQualityAuditTrailImage (string, required): Low quality audit trail image data.
  - userAgent (string, required): User agent string from FaceTec SDK.
- imageDepiction (string, required): Enum: "selfie" "front". This field only applies to the 'facetec' provider and is required. It defines the image depiction in the process that is used to compare against the images captured in `facetecEnrollment`.
- rAuthorityId (string, optional): Id of the registration authority where the VideoID will be sent to be verified by an agent. If not set, it will use the default value set in your Signicat Account.

Responses:
- 200: The request was successfully sent.
- 204: The request was successfully sent (only applies to the 'readid' and 'webid' providers).
- 400: The request cannot be fulfilled due to bad syntax.
- 401: The Bearer token provided in the Authorization header was not valid.
- 404: The resource requested cannot be found.

Request Sample (Payload):
Content type: application/json
{
  "facetecEnrollment": {
    "faceScan": "BAGZzkV3wyl4CP/CYnAiaq1VfwbcAMM02pohZ8a5Mm5v3",
    "auditTrailImage": "/9j/4AAQSkZJRgABAQAAAQABAAD",
    "lowQualityAuditTrailImage": "/9j/4AAQSkZJRgABAQAAAQABAAD",
    "userAgent": "facetec|sdk|android|com.signicat.assure|dvFMSBMcyjjUB7dvR0lFWsOHoNiBsLDh|C71F69E46DF67349|SM-G970F|9.4.1|pt_PT|pt|621c18e4-5462-43a0-ac2b-346ac68a9270"
  },
  "imageDepiction": "selfie",
  "rAuthorityId": "11a56f16-6f19-4282-8f2d-3749b86471d5"
}

Response Sample (200):
Content type: application/json
{
  "processId": "8afb3ac6-6780-42e4-bbc2-3713e2f6d97c",
  "status": "processing"
}
```

TITLE: AuthnResponse Example with eHerkenning
DESCRIPTION: This XML snippet demonstrates a typical SAML 2.0 AuthnResponse generated after a successful authentication via eHerkenning. It includes essential elements like Issuer, Status, Subject, Conditions, and AttributeStatement, which contain user and session information.

```

</saml2:Attribute>

</saml2:Attribute>
</saml2:AttributeStatement>
<saml2:AuthnStatementAuthnInstant="2023-12-11T12:35:48.264Z"SessionIndex="14779d0d-08bb-4929-95a2-499363b122f7">
<saml2:AuthnContext>

</saml2:AuthnContext>
</saml2:AuthnStatement>
</saml2:Assertion>
</saml2p:Response>

TITLE: Fetch User Profile Script (Node.js)
DESCRIPTION: A Node.js script to fetch user profile data from the Signicat UserInfo endpoint. It makes a GET request to the UserInfo URL with an access token and parses the JSON response to extract user claims like user_id, name, given_name, and family_name.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/connectors/auth0-integration

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
function(accessToken, ctx, callback){
    const profile ={};
    request.get(
{
url:'https://<YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN>/auth/open/connect/userinfo',
headers={
'Authorization':'Bearer '+ accessToken,
}
},
(err, resp, body)=>{
if(err){
returncallback(err);
}
if(resp.statusCode !==200){
returncallback(newError(body));
}
let bodyParsed;
try{
        bodyParsed =JSON.parse(body);
}
catch(jsonError){
returncallback(newError(body));
}
const profile ={
user_id: bodyParsed.sub,
name: bodyParsed.name,
given_name: bodyParsed.given_name,
family_name: bodyParsed.family_name
};
callback(null, profile);
}
);
}
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenID Connect for Norwegian BankID Integration
DESCRIPTION: Provides guidance on using the OpenID Connect (OIDC) protocol for integrating Norwegian BankID. Covers OIDC flows, required parameters, and how to obtain user information.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/nbid/integration-guide

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenID Connect Flow:

1.  **Authorization Request**:
    Redirect the user's browser to the Signicat authorization endpoint with the following parameters:
    - `client_id`: Your Signicat client ID.
    - `redirect_uri`: The URI Signicat will redirect to after authentication.
    - `response_type`: Typically `code` for the authorization code flow.
    - `scope`: Specifies the requested permissions (e.g., `openid`, `profile`).
    - `state`: An optional parameter to maintain state and prevent CSRF attacks.
    - `nonce`: An optional parameter to mitigate replay attacks.

    Example URL:
    `https://<signicat-auth-endpoint>/oauth2/authorize?client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&redirect_uri=YOUR_REDIRECT_URI&response_type=code&scope=openid%20profile&state=OPTIONAL_STATE&nonce=OPTIONAL_NONCE`

2.  **Callback and Authorization Code**:
    After successful authentication, Signicat redirects the user back to your `redirect_uri` with an authorization `code` and the `state` parameter.

3.  **Token Exchange**:
    Your backend server exchanges the authorization `code` for an `access_token` and optionally an `id_token` by making a POST request to the Signicat token endpoint.
    - `grant_type`: `authorization_code`
    - `code`: The received authorization code.
    - `redirect_uri`: The same redirect URI used in the authorization request.
    - `client_id`: Your Signicat client ID.
    - `client_secret`: Your Signicat client secret.

4.  **User Information**:
    Use the `access_token` to retrieve user information by making a GET request to the Signicat userinfo endpoint.
```

CODE:
```
https://<YOUR_SIGNICAT_DOMAIN>/auth/open/connect/authorize?

  &redirect_uri=<REDIRECT_URI>  
  &scope=openid%20profile%20idp-id  
  &state=<STATE>  
  &code_challenge=ABC123  
  &code_challenge_method=S256  
  &acr_values=idp:email-otp  
  &login_hint=email:email%40example.com

TITLE: Signicat ReuseID Onboarding API Documentation
DESCRIPTION: Documentation for the POST /reuseid/id-onboardings endpoint, which starts a new onboarding session. It includes details on the request body schema for eidProviderOptions, specifying document types and default selections, as well as possible response codes and sample responses.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/reuseid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
post/reuseid/id-onboardings
https://api.signicat.com/reuseid/id-onboardings

Request Body schema: application/json
eidProviderOptions |  object An object that contains parameters for deciding what kind of documents can be used, and which document should be the default. 
  * If not specified, then all ID documents that our VideoID solution supports will be available as an option for the end-user. 
  * If only one specific document is to be used, then you can specify this with `docType`. 
  * If multiple documents are to be available, then you can specify this with `docTypes`. 

**Note** : When multiple `docTypes` are specified, we recommend that you provide a `defaultId`. This is the first option shown to the user.  
---|---  
| docType |  integer A parameter to specify a single document type that you want to be used by the end-user.  
---|---  
docTypes |  Array of integers A parameter to specify multiple document types that you want to be available for the end-user to choose from.  
defaultId |  integer A parameter to specify the default document type that you want to be shown to the end-user, when multiple document types are specified. This can only be used when `docTypes` has been provided. **Note** : If not set, then the default is the lowest integer.  

### Responses
**200**
Successful response
**403**
Forbidden
**422**
Unprocessable Entity (WebDAV)

###  Request samples 
  * Payload

Content type
application/json
Copy
Expand all  Collapse all 
`{
  *  "eidProviderOptions": { 
    *  "docType": 138, 
 
    *  "docTypes": [ 
      *  138,
 
      * 123
  ], 
 
    *  "defaultId": 138 
  }

 }`
###  Response samples 
  * 200
  * 403
  * 422

Content type
application/json
Copy
Expand all  Collapse all 
`{
  *  "data": { 
    *  "status": "Pending", 
 
    *  "transactionId": "94099e7e-b391-45fb-9404-b54682f16d03", 
 
    *  "userId": "7f1994f0-5fed-4e0f-a8e2-64da520a09cb", 
 
    *  "activationCode": "2005468691", 
 
    *  "dossierId": "41ff5755-4ece-42cf-b7de-3efd0181ba88", 
 
    *  "processId": "8be8325a-9654-4165-a56f-0d1ccdc3bd3e"
  }

 }`
```

TITLE: Check MitID App Installation (Android)
DESCRIPTION: Verifies if the MitID app is installed on an Android device. Requires specific package name and manifest configuration for Android 11+.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/integration-guide/app-switching

LANGUAGE: java
CODE:
```
public boolean deviceHasMitIDApp() {
  try {
    getPackageManager().getPackageInfo("dk.mitid.codeapp.android", 0);
    return true;
  } catch (PackageManager.NameNotFoundException e) {
    return false;
  }
}
```

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<manifest>
<queries>
<package android:name="dk.mitid.app.android"/>
</queries>
<application/>
</manifest>
```

TITLE: Signicat Mint API - Instance Management
DESCRIPTION: Provides endpoints for retrieving and managing instances within the Signicat Mint API. This includes listing all instances, fetching an instance by its ID, and downloading associated files.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/mint

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  /flows/instances (GET)
    Description: Lists all instances for all flows belonging to a Signicat account. Allows filtering by status, correlation ID, order, search term, offset, and limit.
    Authorizations: Bearer
    Query Parameters:
      status: string (FlowStatus) - Enum: "Idle", "Running", "Finished", "Suspended", "Faulted", "Cancelled"
      correlationId: string
      orderby: string (InstanceOrderByDto) - Enum: "Started", "LastExecuted", "Finished"
      searchTerm: string
      offset: integer <int32>
      limit: integer <int32>
    Responses:
      200: OK
      401: Unauthorized
      404: Not Found

  /flows/instances/{instanceId} (GET)
    Description: Retrieves an instance for a given instanceId.
    Authorizations: Bearer
    Path Parameters:
      instanceId: string - The ID of the instance.
    Responses:
      200: OK. Returns the flow with the passed ID.
      400: Bad Request
      401: Unauthorized
      404: Not Found

  /flows/instances/{instanceId}/files/{referenceId}/download (GET)
    Description: Downloads a specific file associated with an instance.
    Authorizations: Bearer
    Path Parameters:
      instanceId: string - ID of the instance.
      referenceId: string - Unique reference of the file.
    Responses:
      200: OK
      400: Bad Request
      401: Unauthorized

  /flows/instances/{instanceId}/files/download (GET)
    Description: Downloads a zip file containing all files for a given instance.
    Authorizations: Bearer
    Path Parameters:
      instanceId: string - ID of the instance.
    Responses:
      200: OK
      400: Bad Request
      401: Unauthorized

  /flows/instances/{id}/resume (POST)
    Description: Resumes a specific instance by its ID.
    Authorizations: Bearer
    Path Parameters:
      id: string - ID of the instance to resume.
    Request Body Schema:
      application/json-patch+json, application/json, text/json, application/*+json
      input: object or null
        activityId: string or null
    Responses:
      200: OK
      400: Bad Request
      401: Unauthorized
      404: Not Found
      408: Request Timeout

  /flows/instances/{id}/resume/approval (POST)
    Description: Approves a specific instance by its ID.
    Authorizations: Bearer
    Path Parameters:
      id: string - ID of the instance to resume.
    Request Body Schema:
      application/json-patch+json, application/json, text/json, application/*+json
      input: object (ResumeApprovalInstanceInputDto)
        activityId: string or null
    Responses:
      200: OK
      400: Bad Request
      401: Unauthorized
      404: Not Found
      408: Request Timeout
```

TITLE: Signicat Theming Service - How Theming Works
DESCRIPTION: Explains the functionality of the Theming service, including theme creation, application scope, and inheritance.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/theming

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Theming Mechanics:
  - Theme creation via Theming service in Signicat Dashboard.
  - Themes affect only end-user content appearance, not the Signicat Dashboard.
  - Application Scope:
    - Account level: Can be applied to an account or domain level.
    - Domain level: Can apply one or more themes.
  - Inheritance:
    - A theme set at the account level becomes the default for child domains.
```

TITLE: SAML 2.0 Metadata with HTTP-POST Binding
DESCRIPTION: Example SAML 2.0 metadata XML for a Service Provider (SP) using the HTTP-POST binding. This includes entity ID, signature, key descriptor with X.509 certificate, and Assertion Consumer Service (ACS) endpoint for POST binding.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/saml-2-0/saml-metadata

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<md:EntityDescriptor xmlns:md="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:metadata"ID="_9ef5602b6f9ed8b75334f563f91322d2"
entityID=ENTITY_ID>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
        XML_SIGNATURE
</ds:Signature>
<md:SPSSODescriptorAuthnRequestsSigned="true"WantAssertionsSigned="true"
protocolSupportEnumeration="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol">
<md:KeyDescriptoruse="signing">
<ds:KeyInfoxmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
<ds:KeyName>KEY_NAME</ds:KeyName>
<ds:X509Data>
<ds:X509Certificate>
                        X509_CERTIFICATE
</ds:X509Certificate>
</ds:X509Data>
</ds:KeyInfo>
</md:KeyDescriptor>
<md:AssertionConsumerServiceBinding="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:bindings:HTTP-POST"
Location="https://*SP_APP_DOMAIN*/saml/acs"index="0"
isDefault="true"/>
</md:SPSSODescriptor>
<md:Organization>
<md:OrganizationNamexml:lang="en">ORG_NAME</md:OrganizationName>
<md:OrganizationDisplayNamexml:lang="en">ORG_DISPLAY_NAME</md:OrganizationDisplayName>
<md:OrganizationURLxml:lang="en">ORG_URL</md:OrganizationURL>
</md:Organization>
</md:EntityDescriptor>
```

TITLE: Check MitID App Installation (iOS)
DESCRIPTION: Checks for the presence of the MitID production app on iOS using a URL scheme. Requires 'mitid-app' in LSApplicationQueriesSchemes.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/mitid/integration-guide/app-switching

LANGUAGE: swift
CODE:
```
func canOpenMitIDApp() -> Bool {
  guard let url = URL(string: "https://appswitch.mitid.nets.eu/.well-known/apple-app-site-association”) else {
    return false
  }
  return UIApplication.shared.canOpenUrl(url)
}
```

TITLE: Start Authentication
DESCRIPTION: Initiates an authentication process for a specified user on their device. Requires user ID and optionally device details and operation properties.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/mobileid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIMethod: POST
Endpoint: /mobileid/core/authentications
URL: https://api.signicat.com/mobileid/core/authentications

Request Body (application/json):
  userId (string, required, non-empty): The ID of the user performing the operation (UUID format).
  device (object, optional): Device details. For registration, only 'name' is allowed if specified. For authentication/signing, mandatory unless broadcast is enabled.
    id (string): The ID of the device.
    name (string): The name of the device.
  tags (Array of strings, optional): Tags for callback event filtering.
  operationProperties (object, optional): Properties for carrying out the operation.
    sessionTimeout (string): Timeout for the session.

Responses:
  201: The request to start authentication was successful.
  400: Bad Request. The server cannot find the requested resource.
  403: Forbidden. The user is not authorised to perform this operation.

Request Sample:
{
  "userId": "0e99b25c-abde-4553-973b-8d94d49cd87e",
  "device": {
    "id": "20874199-f4d1-4e9d-86ee-dd4a46030acb"
  },
  "operationProperties": {
    "sessionTimeout": "90000"
  },
  "tags": [
    "some tag",
    "another tag"
  ]
}
```

TITLE: Signicat Theme Application (Domain Level)
DESCRIPTION: Explains the process of applying themes to individual domains within an account, including the recommended order of operations to prevent data loss. Also covers applying multiple themes to a single domain.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/theming

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Theming Service - Domain Level Application:
  Prerequisites:
    - Account Theme: Set the custom theme for the account first.
    - Domain Themes: Set custom themes for specific domains afterward.
  Recommended Order:
    1. Set account theme.
    2. Set domain themes.
    *Applying account theme after domain themes will overwrite domain settings.*
  Steps to Set Custom Theme for a Domain:
    1. Enable Domain Themes: Toggle 'Use different themes for domains'.
    2. Select Domain: Choose the target domain from 'Accounts and domains'.
    3. Select Theme: Use the 'Selected theme' dropdown.
    4. Apply Theme: Click 'Apply theme'.
  Steps to Apply Multiple Themes for a Domain:
    1. Enable Domain Themes: Toggle 'Use different themes for domains'.
    2. Select Domain: Choose the target domain.
    3. Enable Multiple Themes: Toggle 'Use multiple themes for this domain'.
    4. Add Themes:
       - Select a theme.
       - Click '+ Add theme'.
       - Repeat for additional themes.
    5. Confirm Application: Click 'Apply multiple themes'.
```

----------------------------------------

----------------------------------------

TITLE: itsme® Integration with OIDC
DESCRIPTION: This section details the process of integrating with itsme® using the OpenID Connect (OIDC) protocol. It covers the necessary configurations and steps to establish a secure authentication flow.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/itsme/integration

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Integration with OIDC:
  Description: Guides on integrating with itsme® using the OpenID Connect (OIDC) protocol.
  Key Concepts:
    - Relying Party (RP): Your application that initiates the authentication request.
    - OpenID Provider (OP): itsme® acts as the OpenID Provider.
    - Authentication Request:
      - Parameters:
        - client_id: Your application's identifier.
        - redirect_uri: The URI where the user is redirected after authentication.
        - scope: Defines the requested permissions (e.g., openid, profile).
        - response_type: Typically 'code' for authorization code flow.
        - nonce: A unique identifier to mitigate replay attacks.
        - state: An opaque value used to maintain state between the request and callback.
    - Token Endpoint:
      - POST request to exchange authorization code for tokens.
      - Parameters:
        - grant_type: 'authorization_code'.
        - code: The authorization code received.
        - redirect_uri: Must match the one in the initial request.
        - client_id: Your application's identifier.
        - client_secret: Your application's secret.
    - UserInfo Endpoint:
      - GET request to retrieve user profile information.
      - Requires an Access Token in the Authorization header.
  Example Flow:
    1. RP redirects user to itsme® authorization endpoint.
    2. User authenticates with itsme®.
    3. itsme® redirects user back to RP's redirect_uri with an authorization code.
    4. RP exchanges the authorization code for tokens at the token endpoint.
    5. RP uses the ID token and potentially calls the UserInfo endpoint.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: SAML 2.0 Metadata with HTTP-Artifact Binding
DESCRIPTION: Example SAML 2.0 metadata XML for a Service Provider (SP) using the HTTP-Artifact binding. This includes entity ID, signature, key descriptor with X.509 certificate, and Assertion Consumer Service (ACS) endpoint for Artifact binding.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/eid-hub/saml-2-0/saml-metadata

LANGUAGE: xml
CODE:
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<md:EntityDescriptor xmlns:md="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:metadata"ID="_9ef5602b6f9ed8b75334f563f91322d2"
entityID=ENTITY_ID>
<ds:Signature xmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
        XML_SIGNATURE
</ds:Signature>
<md:SPSSODescriptorAuthnRequestsSigned="true"WantAssertionsSigned="true"
protocolSupportEnumeration="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:protocol">
<md:KeyDescriptoruse="signing">
<ds:KeyInfoxmlns:ds="http://www.w3.org/2000/09/xmldsig#">
<ds:KeyName>KEY_NAME</ds:KeyName>
<ds:X509Data>
<ds:X509Certificate>
                        X509_CERTIFICATE
</ds:X509Certificate>
</ds:X509Data>
</ds:KeyInfo>
</md:KeyDescriptor>
<md:AssertionConsumerServiceBinding="urn:oasis:names:tc:SAML:2.0:bindings:HTTP-Artifact"
Location="https://*SP_APP_DOMAIN*/saml/acs"index="0"
isDefault="true"/>
</md:SPSSODescriptor>
<md:Organization>
<md:OrganizationNamexml:lang="en">ORG_NAME</md:OrganizationName>
<md:OrganizationDisplayNamexml:lang="en">ORG_DISPLAY_NAME</md:OrganizationDisplayName>
<md:OrganizationURLxml:lang="en">ORG_URL</md:OrganizationURL>
</md:Organization>
</md:EntityDescriptor>
```

TITLE: Get User Transactions (GET)
DESCRIPTION: Retrieves a list of device transactions for a specific end-user. Supports pagination with limit and offset parameters. The userId must be a valid UUID.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/mobileid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  GET /users/{userId}/transactions
  https://api.signicat.com/mobileid/core/users/{userId}/transactions

  Parameters:
    userId (string, required, UUID): The ID of the user for whom to retrieve transactions.
    deviceId (string, optional): Use only if a broadcast operation results in an error.
    limit (string, optional): Number of device transactions per page. Range: 1-100. Default: 100.
    offset (string, optional): Transaction ID to start the response from. If not provided, starts from the first transaction.

  Responses:
    200: Successfully fetched the transactions for the end-user’s devices.
    400: Invalid request.
    403: Forbidden. The user is not authorised to perform this operation.
    404: Not found. The server cannot find the requested resource.
    500: Internal server error.

  Response samples (200):
    Content type: application/json
    {
      "previous": "/users/d910994d-80b2-4125-a6b1-062b5b2f43ba/transactions?limit=1&offset=39277b72-53c2-4780-ad56-a8c8d8a33542",
      "next": "/users/d910994d-80b2-4125-a6b1-062b5b2f43ba/transactions?limit=1&offset=a1c66944-e5e3-46e3-ba36-750622205ef3",
      "limit": 1,
      "transactions": [
        {
          "transactionId": "c5c25109-53ab-4f76-9724-93f77a9b4a7d",
          "ref": "/authentications/mapped-from-c5c25109-53ab-4f76-9724-93f77a9b4a7d",
          "operationType": "AUTHENTICATION",
          "state": "SUCCESS",
          "created": "2023-08-11T11:30:05.000Z",
          "expires": "2023-08-11T11:31:05.000Z",
          "deviceId": "db441aa4-dd01-4bf7-8795-f75a94ec8d61"
        }
      ]
    }
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Onboarding API
DESCRIPTION: The ReuseID Onboarding API facilitates operations related to the onboarding flow, including starting and retrieving information about a ReuseID session. The onboarding process involves creating a MobileID user, registering a MobileID device, and performing a VideoID proofing.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/reuseid

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Onboarding API
The ReuseID Onboarding API provides you with operations related to the onboarding flow, such as starting and getting information about a ReuseID session.
About the onboarding flow
  1. The onboarding flow creates a MobileID user and initiates a MobileID device registration.
  2. Once the end-user has confirmed the activation code, their device is registered to their account and the VideoID session is started.
  3. After the end-user has successfully gone through the VideoID process, the flow updates the user information with the data from the VideoID process.
```

TITLE: Signicat FTN Integration Protocols
DESCRIPTION: Overview of authentication protocols supported by Signicat's FTN implementation. Recommends OIDC for its industry standard compliance and easier session management compared to SAML 2.0 or the REST API.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/ftn/integration-guide/prerequisites

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Protocol Support:
  - OIDC (OpenID Connect): Recommended for industry standard compliance and simplified user session management.
  - SAML 2.0: More complex to implement, often requires an existing federation agent.
  - Signicat Authentication REST API: Offers high flexibility and ease of setup.
```

TITLE: Check DNS Status API (Utility)
DESCRIPTION: Checks the DNS setup status for a given domain and certificate kind. This is a utility endpoint that does not require a pre-existing domain ID. Returns 200 OK on success or 404 Not Found.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/domain-management

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
POST /check-dns-setup
https://api.signicat.com/domain-management/check-dns-setup

Request Body (application/json):
{
  "domain": "string" (required, non-empty): The domain to check.
  "certificateKind": "string" (required, Enum: "LetsEncrypt", "Csr", "Custom"): The type of certificate.
}

Responses:
- 200 OK: Returns the DNS status information.
- 404 Not Found: Indicates an issue with the request or domain.
```

TITLE: Get Process API Reference
DESCRIPTION: Provides details on the 'getProcess' API operation, including its purpose, response structure, and status codes. It outlines the information available for a verification process.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/id-document-and-biometric-verification/services/process

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
APIDOC:
  operationId: getProcess
  tags:
    - Processes
  summary: Retrieve a process
  description: Use this service to retrieve important information about a verification process:
    - The provider used (`signicatvideoid`, `onfido`, `readid` etc.).
    - The process type (`high`, `selfie`, `video` etc.).
    - The status of the process (`accepted`, `rejected` etc.).
    - When the process started and when it was last updated (`createdAt`, `updatedAt`).
    - Provider-specific information about different verification features used in the verification (`facialSimilarity`, `documentVerification` etc.).
    - The final result with end-user information (`firstName`, `lastName`, `dateOfBirth` etc.).
  responses:
    '200':
      description: OK
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            type: object
            properties:
              provider:
                type: string
                description: The provider used for the verification.
              status:
                type: string
                description: The current status of the process.
              processId:
                type: string
                format: uuid
                description: The unique identifier for the process.
              createdAt:
                type: string
                format: date-time
                description: The timestamp when the process was created.
              updatedAt:
                type: string
                format: date-time
                description: The timestamp when the process was last updated.
              facialSimilarity:
                type: object
                description: Provider-specific information for facial similarity verification.
              documentVerification:
                type: object
                description: Provider-specific information for document verification.
              firstName:
                type: string
                description: The first name of the end-user.
              lastName:
                type: string
                description: The last name of the end-user.
              dateOfBirth:
                type: string
                format: date
                description: The date of birth of the end-user.
    '400':
      description: Bad Request
    '401':
      description: Unauthorized
    '404':
      description: Not Found
    '500':
      description: Internal Server Error
```

TITLE: Initialize and Run Onfido SDK (Java)
DESCRIPTION: This code snippet demonstrates how to initialize and run the Onfido SDK in a Java Android application. It requires an authorization token obtained from the Assure API and allows for custom flow configuration.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/id-document-and-biometric-verification/provider-specific-integrations/onfido

LANGUAGE: Java
CODE:
```
OnfidoConfig config = new OnfidoConfig.Builder(activity)
  .withSDKToken(authorization) // this is the authorization you received from Assure API
  .withCustomFlow(steps) // these steps will have to be configured by you depending on the document you're using and the processType
  .build();
Onfido onfido = OnfidoFactory.create(activity).getClient();
onfido.startActivityForResult(activity, ONFIDO_PROCESS_REQUEST_ID, config); // ONFIDO_PROCESS_REQUEST_ID is the ID that comes to the onActivityResult method.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Authentication REST API for Norwegian BankID
DESCRIPTION: Details the REST API endpoints and methods for authenticating users with Norwegian BankID. This includes information on request parameters, response formats, and error handling for authentication flows.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/identity-methods/nbid/integration-guide

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Authentication REST API:
  Endpoint: /v1/authentication
  Methods:
    POST:
      Initiates an authentication request.
      Parameters:
        - client_id: Your Signicat client ID (string)
        - redirect_uri: The URI to redirect to after authentication (string)
        - scope: Requested scopes (e.g., 'openid profile') (string)
        - response_type: Type of response (e.g., 'code') (string)
        - state: Opaque value used to maintain state between the request and callback (string, optional)
        - nonce: String value used to associate a client session with an ID Token, and to mitigate replay attacks (string, optional)
      Returns:
        - authorization_url: The URL to redirect the user to for authentication (string)
        - error: Description of the error if the request failed (string, optional)
      Example:
        POST /v1/authentication
        Content-Type: application/json
        {
          "client_id": "your_client_id",
          "redirect_uri": "https://your.app/callback",
          "scope": "openid profile",
          "response_type": "code",
          "state": "some_state"
        }

  Endpoint: /v1/token
  Methods:
    POST:
      Exchanges an authorization code for an access token.
      Parameters:
        - grant_type: Must be 'authorization_code' (string)
        - code: The authorization code received from the authentication endpoint (string)
        - redirect_uri: The redirect URI used in the initial authentication request (string)
        - client_id: Your Signicat client ID (string)
        - client_secret: Your Signicat client secret (string)
      Returns:
        - access_token: The access token for making API calls (string)
        - token_type: The type of token (e.g., 'Bearer') (string)
        - expires_in: The lifetime in seconds of the access token (integer)
        - id_token: The ID token containing user information (string, optional)
        - error: Description of the error if the request failed (string, optional)
      Example:
        POST /v1/token
        Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded
        grant_type=authorization_code&code=your_auth_code&redirect_uri=https://your.app/callback&client_id=your_client_id&client_secret=your_client_secret

  Endpoint: /v1/userinfo
  Methods:
    GET:
      Retrieves user information using an access token.
      Headers:
        - Authorization: Bearer <access_token>
      Returns:
        - User claims based on the requested scopes (JSON object)
        - error: Description of the error if the request failed (string, optional)
      Example:
        GET /v1/userinfo
        Authorization: Bearer your_access_token
```

TITLE: Signicat Theming Service - Product Support
DESCRIPTION: Lists products that support the Signicat Theming service and provides alternatives for products that do not, such as MitID.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/docs/theming

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Product Support:
  - eID Hub: Supports Theming. For MitID, use Advanced graphical profile (add-on).
  - ID Document and Biometric Verification: Supports Theming.
  - Signicat Mint: Supports Theming.
  - MobileID: Supports Theming.
  - Electronic Signature API:
    - Enterprise Electronic Signature API: Relies on Graphical profiles editor. Contact key account manager for ordering or modification.
    - Express Electronic Signature API: Refer to Theming guide in Express Signature documentation.
    - MitID Express or Enterprise: Refer to Advanced graphical profile (add-on) guide.

TITLE: Sign API - Create Signing Session
DESCRIPTION: Defines the schema and provides an example for creating a signing session via the Signicat API. It includes details on required fields, data types, and constraints for various parameters like title, signText, documents, senderDisplayName, and redirect settings.

SOURCE: https://developer.signicat.com/apis/electronic-signing/sign-api-v2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
post/signing-sessions
https://api.signicat.com/sign/signing-sessions

Request Body schema: application/json
required
Array ([ 1 .. 100 ] items)
titlerequired |  string <= 255 characters   
---|---  
signText |  string <= 2048 characters   
dueDate |  string <date-time> The deadline for signing the document(s). Can be a maximum of 30 days into the future from the current date.  
documentsrequired |  Array of objects (SessionDocument)  [ 1 .. 50 ] items   
senderDisplayName |  string <= 255 characters  The name of the entity that requested the signature. Displayed while signing.  
externalReference |  string or null <= 1024 characters  Custom identifier for linking the signing session to your internal process. Passed back in redirect URLs.  
signingSetuprequired |  Array of objects (SigningSetup)  = 1 items  The user interaction setups for this signing session describing which IDPs are available for the end-user.  
subsequentTo |  Array of strings <uuid> <= 50 items [ items <uuid > ] IDs of signing sessions that must be signed before this one.  
packageTo |  Array of strings (PackageType)  <= 5 items  Items Value: "PADES_CONTAINER" A list of formats the signing session should be packaged to when signed.  
signer |  object (Signer)  The intended signer of the signing Session.  
preAuthentication |  object (PreAuthentication)  Sets up authentication of the signer before presenting documents.  
ui |  object (Ui)  Defines UI settings for the signing session.  
redirectSettings |  object (RedirectSettings)  Defines URLs for redirects.  

Responses
**201**
The signing session was created.
```

LANGUAGE: JSON
CODE:
```
[
  {
    "title": "Business Process",
    "signText": "Please sign this document",
